Background services drain in reverse order of startup\\n4. gRPC server uses select pattern: waits for graceful stop or timeout (lines 192-197)\\n5. All service goroutines stop before process exit\\n\\n### Common Patterns\\n\\n**Signal Handling Pattern:**\\nAll three services:\\n- Use buffered signal channels (capacity 1-2) via `signal.Notify()`\\n- Register both SIGTERM and SIGINT (Interrupt)\\n- Handle graceful shutdown in separate goroutines\\n- Support immediate exit on second signal (in Kubernetes) or timeout-based forceful shutdown (in Grafana/Prometheus)\\n\\n**Timeout Implementation:**\\nAll implementations use `context.WithTimeout()` or `context.WithCancel()` for shutdown coordination:\\n- Kubernetes: 60-second request drain timeout + 70-second initial delay\\n- Prometheus: 5-second component shutdown timeout\\n- Grafana: 30-second main shutdown + component-specific timeouts\\n\\n**Connection Draining:**\\nDraining strategies vary:\\n- Kubernetes: Drains non-long-running in-flight requests within timeout, then closes HTTP server\\n- Prometheus: Uses actor-group pattern for ordered component shutdown, notifier supports optional queue drain\\n- Grafana: Background service manager handles cascading shutdown, gRPC server uses timeout-based graceful stop\"\n   132→}\n   133→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
